ChatGPT said:
Great! At this point, you have two aligned datasets for your multimodal model:

Image features: X_img_train and X_img_test

Voice features: Xv_train_aligned and Xv_test_aligned

Labels: y_img_train and y_img_test

Now, to merge them for multimodal training, you generally have two options depending on how your model is designed:

Option 1: Use a multi-input model (recommended)
Instead of literally concatenating features (which is tricky for images + 1D vectors), you feed each modality into its own branch and merge them later in the model. Example in Keras:

from tensorflow.keras.layers import Input, Dense, Flatten, Concatenate
from tensorflow.keras.models import Model
from tensorflow.keras.applications import ResNet50

# --- Image branch ---
image_input = Input(shape=(224, 224, 3))
base_model = ResNet50(weights='imagenet', include_top=False, input_tensor=image_input)
x_img = Flatten()(base_model.output)
x_img = Dense(128, activation='relu')(x_img)

# --- Voice branch ---
voice_input = Input(shape=(22,))  # Xv_train_aligned has shape (num_samples, 22)
x_voice = Dense(64, activation='relu')(voice_input)
x_voice = Dense(32, activation='relu')(x_voice)

# --- Merge branches ---
merged = Concatenate()([x_img, x_voice])
output = Dense(1, activation='sigmoid')(merged)  # or softmax for multi-class

# --- Model ---
final_model = Model(inputs=[image_input, voice_input], outputs=output)
final_model.compile(optimizer='adam', loss='binary_crossentropy', metrics=['accuracy'])

# --- Train ---
final_model.fit(
    [X_img_train, Xv_train_aligned], 
    y_img_train,
    validation_data=([X_img_test, Xv_test_aligned], y_img_test),
    epochs=10,
    batch_size=16
)
✅ Advantages:

Each modality is handled properly (images use CNN, voice uses dense layers).

Flexible, easier to tune.

Option 2: Flatten and concatenate manually
If you want to combine all features into one vector, you can flatten image features (e.g., using a pre-trained CNN to get embeddings) and concatenate with voice features:

# Assume X_img_train_embedded is extracted image features (e.g., from ResNet)
X_train_merged = np.concatenate([X_img_train_embedded, Xv_train_aligned], axis=1)
X_test_merged  = np.concatenate([X_img_test_embedded, Xv_test_aligned], axis=1)
Then train a single Dense network on X_train_merged.

⚠️ Note: For images, flattening raw pixels is inefficient; it’s better to extract embeddings first.

So the next step for you is:

Decide if you want multi-input model (recommended) or feature concatenation.

If multi-input: build the model as above.

If concatenation: extract image embeddings first, then merge with voice features.

I can write a full working example using your current X_img_train and Xv_train_aligned for multimodal training next if you want.

after all this weather the image and voice dataset is merged 
ChatGPT said:
Exactly! When you use a multi-input model like we discussed, the datasets are merged conceptually within the model, but not literally concatenated into a single array. Here's what happens:

How the merge works
Two separate inputs:

Image data (X_img_train) goes through the image branch (e.g., CNN like ResNet).

Voice data (Xv_train_aligned) goes through the voice branch (Dense layers).

Feature extraction per modality:

Each branch transforms its input into a feature vector (image embeddings, voice embeddings).

Concatenation inside the model:

After each branch processes its input, the model merges the outputs using a Concatenate() layer.

From this point, the model sees a combined feature representation of both modalities.

Final prediction:

The merged features go through Dense layers to make a final prediction.

✅ Key point
Before the model: X_img_train and Xv_train_aligned are separate.

Inside the model: They are merged at the concatenation layer.

You do not need to merge them manually; the model handles it.

If you want, I can draw a simple diagram showing how image and voice data are merged in the multi-input model—it makes it super clear visually.

Step A: Capture inputs
Image (handwriting/facial scan):

from PIL import Image
import cv2
import numpy as np

# Capture from webcam (example)
cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
ret, frame = cap.read()
if ret:
    img = cv2.resize(frame, (224, 224))  # same size as training images

Voice (speech recording):

import sounddevice as sd
import librosa

duration = 5  # seconds
fs = 16000    # sample rate

print("Recording...")
audio = sd.rec(int(duration * fs), samplerate=fs, channels=1)
sd.wait()
audio = audio.flatten()

# Extract features like MFCC (used in X_voice)
mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=audio, sr=fs, n_mfcc=22)
mfccs = np.mean(mfccs.T, axis=0)  # shape (22,)
mfccs = mfccs.reshape(1, -1)      # add batch dimension
Step B: Make prediction
# Load your trained model
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
final_model = load_model("multimodal_model.h5")

# Predict
prediction = final_model.predict([img, mfccs])
prediction_class = (prediction > 0.5).astype(int)

if prediction_class[0][0] == 1:
    print("Prediction: Parkinson's disease detected")
else:
    print("Prediction: No Parkinson's disease detected")

Sure! Let me explain exactly what the output of your multimodal Parkinson’s detection model will look like and how to interpret it.

1️⃣ Type of Output
Since your model is likely using binary classification (sigmoid activation in the last layer), the output will be:

prediction = final_model.predict([image_input, voice_input])
print(prediction)
The prediction will be a floating-point number between 0 and 1.

Shape will be (1, 1) if predicting for a single user sample.

Example:

Prediction Value	Interpretation
0.05	Very likely No Parkinson’s disease
0.45	Leaning towards No Parkinson’s, but uncertain
0.60	Leaning towards Parkinson’s disease, borderline
0.95	Very likely Parkinson’s disease
2️⃣ Converting to Class Labels
Usually, we threshold at 0.5:

prediction_class = (prediction > 0.5).astype(int)
0 → No Parkinson’s disease

1 → Parkinson’s disease detected

Example:

if prediction_class[0][0] == 1:
    print("Prediction: Parkinson's disease detected")
else:
    print("Prediction: No Parkinson's disease detected")
3️⃣ What happens internally
Image branch processes the user’s image → extracts image features.

Voice branch processes the user’s speech → extracts voice features.

The features are merged in the model.

The final Dense layer with sigmoid produces a number 0-1, representing probability of Parkinson’s disease.

The closer the number is to 1, the more confident the model is that the person has Parkinson’s disease.

4️⃣ Optional: Get Confidence Score
You can also report confidence to the user:

confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}%")
Example output:

Confidence: 87.32%
This helps communicate how sure the model is about the prediction.

ChatGPT said:
Ah! That warning is coming from TensorFlow/Keras and it’s informational, not an error. Let me explain clearly:

Why it appears
When you do:

final_model.save("multimodal_model.h5")
Keras saves the model in the HDF5 format (.h5), which is older/legacy.

TensorFlow now recommends using the native Keras format (.keras), which is more modern and fully supports all Keras features.

What you should do instead
# Save in modern Keras format
final_model.save("multimodal_model.keras")
This will save the model in the native Keras format.

You can still load it later using:

from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")
✅ Key points
Both .h5 and .keras work for most cases.

Using .keras is recommended for future compatibility, especially if your model has custom layers or multi-input structures.

No changes are needed for your training or prediction code—just the filename extension.

If you want, I can show you a full saving & loading snippet for your multimodal Parkinson’s model in the recommended .keras format so you won’t see this warning again.

ChatGPT said:
Perfect! Let’s go step by step on how to capture real-time image and voice inputs and preprocess them exactly like your training data for Parkinson’s detection.

1️⃣ Capture and preprocess Image input
You can use a webcam to capture the image or allow the user to upload one. Here's an example using OpenCV:

import cv2
import numpy as np

# --- Capture image from webcam ---
cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # 0 = default webcam
print("Please show your image (handwriting/facial) to the camera...")

ret, frame = cap.read()    # Capture one frame
cap.release()              # Release the webcam

if ret:
    # Preprocess the image
    img = cv2.resize(frame, (224, 224))  # Resize to match training input
    img = img / 255.0                     # Normalize pixel values
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)     # Add batch dimension
else:
    print("Failed to capture image")
img shape will be (1, 224, 224, 3) → ready for model input.

✅ If you want image upload instead of webcam:

from PIL import Image

image_path = "user_image.jpg"
img = Image.open(image_path).resize((224, 224))
img = np.array(img)/255.0
img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)
2️⃣ Capture and preprocess Voice input
You can record audio from the microphone and extract features like MFCCs (the same features used in training):

import sounddevice as sd
import librosa
import numpy as np

duration = 5  # seconds
fs = 16000    # sample rate

print("Recording your voice...")
audio = sd.rec(int(duration * fs), samplerate=fs, channels=1)
sd.wait()  # Wait until recording is finished
audio = audio.flatten()  # Convert to 1D array

# --- Extract MFCC features (shape: 22) ---
mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=audio, sr=fs, n_mfcc=22)
mfccs = np.mean(mfccs.T, axis=0)   # Take mean over time frames
mfccs = mfccs.reshape(1, -1)       # Shape (1, 22) → ready for model
mfccs shape (1, 22) → ready for your voice branch in the multimodal model.

3️⃣ Feed both inputs to the model
# Assume your trained model is loaded
# model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")

prediction = model.predict([img, mfccs])
prediction_class = (prediction > 0.5).astype(int)

if prediction_class[0][0] == 1:
    print("Parkinson's disease detected")
else:
    print("No Parkinson's disease detected")

# Optional: show confidence
confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100
print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}%")
✅ Summary

Image input: capture via webcam or upload → resize (224, 224) → normalize /255 → add batch dimension (1, 224, 224, 3).

Voice input: record → extract MFCC (22 features) → mean over frames → reshape (1, 22).

Prediction: feed both inputs to the multimodal model → get result.

ChatGPT said:
Got it! You want to predict Parkinson’s disease from an image captured via webcam. Let me give you a step-by-step Python example for that. This will handle:

Capturing the image from your webcam.

Preprocessing the image (resize + normalize).

Feeding it to your trained model.

Python code for webcam image prediction
import cv2
import numpy as np
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model

# --- Step 1: Load your trained model ---
# Make sure your model is saved in .keras format
model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")

# --- Step 2: Capture image from webcam ---
cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # 0 = default webcam
print("Please show your image (handwriting/facial scan) to the camera...")
ret, frame = cap.read()
cap.release()  # Release webcam

if not ret:
    print("Failed to capture image")
    exit()

# --- Step 3: Preprocess the image ---
img = cv2.resize(frame, (224, 224))  # Resize to match training input
img = img / 255.0                     # Normalize pixel values
img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)     # Add batch dimension (1, 224, 224, 3)

# --- Step 4: Predict using the model ---
# If you also have voice input, you need to pass it as well. 
# For image-only prediction, you may need a separate image-only model.
# Here, assuming your multimodal model requires both:
# If voice input is missing, you can pass zeros or mean values
Xv_dummy = np.zeros((1, 22))  # Replace 22 with your voice feature size

prediction = model.predict([img, Xv_dummy])
prediction_class = (prediction > 0.5).astype(int)

# --- Step 5: Show result ---
if prediction_class[0][0] == 1:
    print("Prediction: Parkinson's disease detected")
else:
    print("Prediction: No Parkinson's disease detected")

confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100
print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}%")
Notes:
Multimodal model requirement:

Your current model expects both image and voice input.

If you want image-only prediction, you should train a separate image-only model, or use a dummy vector for voice features (like Xv_dummy above) so the model can run.

Webcam behavior:

Make sure your camera is working.

Run the script in an environment that supports webcam capture (like local Python, not Google Colab, unless you use Colab’s webcam workaround).

Confidence score:

Shows how sure the model is about its prediction.

Ah! That “Failed to capture image” happens when Python cannot access your webcam. Let’s troubleshoot step by step.

1️⃣ Check webcam index
cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # 0 = default camera
0 is the default webcam.

If you have multiple cameras, try changing it to 1 or 2:

cap = cv2.VideoCapture(1)
2️⃣ Check if OpenCV can open the camera
Add this check right after creating the VideoCapture object:

cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
if not cap.isOpened():
    print("Cannot access the webcam")
    exit()
If it prints "Cannot access the webcam", then the problem is with your camera driver or permissions.

3️⃣ Use a small delay before reading the frame
Sometimes the camera needs a moment to initialize:

import time

cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
time.sleep(2)  # wait 2 seconds for the camera to warm up

ret, frame = cap.read()
cap.release()
4️⃣ Test camera independently
Run a small script to see if your camera works:

import cv2

cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
if not cap.isOpened():
    print("Cannot open camera")
    exit()

while True:
    ret, frame = cap.read()
    if not ret:
        print("Failed to grab frame")
        break
    cv2.imshow("Webcam Test", frame)
    if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
        break

cap.release()
cv2.destroyAllWindows()
This will open a live webcam window.

Press q to close it.

If this works, then your camera is fine, and the original script just needs a slight delay or proper VideoCapture index.

Ah! Now it’s clear: your Python environment cannot access the webcam at all. This explains why every attempt failed. Let’s go over why this happens and what to do.

Camera is being used by another application

import cv2
import time
import numpy as np

cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
time.sleep(2)  # Give camera time to initialize

if not cap.isOpened():
    print("Cannot access the webcam")
    exit()

ret, frame = cap.read()
cap.release()

if ret:
    cv2.imshow("Captured Image", frame)
    cv2.waitKey(0)
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()
else:
    print("Failed to capture frame")
Option B: If using Google Colab
OpenCV cannot access your local webcam.

You need to use Colab’s JavaScript webcam interface:

from google.colab import output
from IPython.display import display, Javascript
import cv2
from google.colab.patches import cv2_imshow

def capture_image():
    display(Javascript('''
        async function capture(){
            const video = document.createElement('video');
            const stream = await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({video: true});
            video.srcObject = stream;
            await video.play();
            const canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
            canvas.width = video.videoWidth;
            canvas.height = video.videoHeight;
            canvas.getContext('2d').drawImage(video, 0, 0);
            const data = canvas.toDataURL('image/jpeg');
            document.body.appendChild(video);
            google.colab.kernel.invokeFunction('notebook.get_image', [data], {});
        }
        capture();
    '''))
Colab method is more complex; usually easier to run locally if you need a webcam.

1️⃣ Capture the image in Colab
The JavaScript snippet I shared allows you to open the webcam in your browser and capture an image.

In Colab, you need a callback function to receive the image from JS into Python:

import base64
import cv2
import numpy as np
from google.colab import output
from IPython.display import display, Javascript
from PIL import Image
import io

# Callback function to get image data from JS
def get_image(data):
    # data is base64 string from JS
    image_bytes = base64.b64decode(data.split(',')[1])
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    img = np.array(img)
    # Resize and normalize like training images
    img = cv2.resize(img, (224, 224))
    img = img / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)
    global captured_image
    captured_image = img

output.register_callback('notebook.get_image', get_image)

# JS to capture webcam image
display(Javascript('''
async function capture(){
    const video = document.createElement('video');
    const stream = await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({video: true});
    video.srcObject = stream;
    await video.play();
    const canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
    canvas.width = video.videoWidth;
    canvas.height = video.videoHeight;
    canvas.getContext('2d').drawImage(video, 0, 0);
    const data = canvas.toDataURL('image/jpeg');
    google.colab.kernel.invokeFunction('notebook.get_image', [data], {});
    stream.getTracks().forEach(track => track.stop());
}
capture();
'''))
✅ After running this, the captured image will be stored in the variable captured_image in Python, ready for prediction.

Here’s a full Colab-ready code snippet that handles both:

# Install necessary packages
!pip install pillow

import cv2
import numpy as np
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from google.colab import output, files
from IPython.display import display, Javascript
from PIL import Image
import io
import base64

# --- Load your trained multimodal model ---
model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")  # Update path if needed

captured_image = None  # Will store the final image

# --- Option 1: Capture image from webcam ---
def get_image(data):
    """Callback function for JS webcam capture"""
    image_bytes = base64.b64decode(data.split(',')[1])
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    img = np.array(img)
    img = cv2.resize(img, (224, 224))
    img = img / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)
    global captured_image
    captured_image = img

output.register_callback('notebook.get_image', get_image)

def capture_from_webcam():
    display(Javascript('''
    async function capture(){
        const video = document.createElement('video');
        const stream = await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({video: true});
        video.srcObject = stream;
        await video.play();
        const canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
        canvas.width = video.videoWidth;
        canvas.height = video.videoHeight;
        canvas.getContext('2d').drawImage(video, 0, 0);
        const data = canvas.toDataURL('image/jpeg');
        google.colab.kernel.invokeFunction('notebook.get_image', [data], {});
        stream.getTracks().forEach(track => track.stop());
    }
    capture();
    '''))
    print("Webcam image captured!")

# --- Option 2: Upload image manually ---
def upload_image():
    uploaded = files.upload()
    for filename in uploaded.keys():
        img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(uploaded[filename]))
        img = np.array(img)
        img = cv2.resize(img, (224, 224))
        img = img / 255.0
        img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)
        global captured_image
        captured_image = img
    print(f"Image {filename} uploaded and processed!")

# --- Function to predict Parkinson's disease ---
def predict(captured_image):
    # Dummy voice input if you don't have real audio
    Xv_dummy = np.zeros((1, 22))  # Replace 22 with your voice feature size

    prediction = model.predict([captured_image, Xv_dummy])
    prediction_class = (prediction > 0.5).astype(int)
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    if prediction_class[0][0] == 1:
        print("Prediction: Parkinson's disease detected")
    else:
        print("Prediction: No Parkinson's disease detected")
    print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}%")

# --- Example usage ---
# Use one of these:
# capture_from_webcam()  # Uncomment to use webcam
# upload_image()         # Uncomment to upload an image manually

# After capturing or uploading, run prediction:
# predict(captured_image)
✅ How to use this in Colab

Uncomment capture_from_webcam() → run → allow browser camera access.

If webcam doesn’t work:

Uncomment upload_image() → run → choose an image file from your computer.

After the image is ready:

Run predict(captured_image) → model outputs prediction + confidence.

This gives you both options in Colab, and the workflow is ready for your Parkinson’s detection project.

ChatGPT said:
Ah! Let’s break down what you’re seeing:

1️⃣ Pillow message
Requirement already satisfied: pillow in /usr/local/lib/python3.12/dist-packages (11.3.0)
This is normal.

It just tells you that the Pillow library (used for image handling) is already installed.

You don’t need to do anything about it. ✅

2️⃣ Keras warning about optimizer
UserWarning: Skipping variable loading for optimizer 'rmsprop', because it has 222 variables whereas the saved optimizer has 442 variables.
This happens when you load a model with load_model() and the optimizer state in the saved model does not match the current model.

Most common causes:

The model was saved with model.save('...') including the optimizer, then you are loading it in a different environment.

You might have updated Keras/TensorFlow versions since saving.

Impact:

Not a critical error.

It only affects continuing training if you want to resume from exactly where you left off.

For inference/prediction, this warning can be safely ignored.

✅ What to do
If your goal is real-time prediction:

model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")
# You can now run model.predict() without issues.
No action needed for the warning.

If you plan to retrain the model, you can recompile it:

model.compile(optimizer='rmsprop', loss='binary_crossentropy', metrics=['accuracy'])
So in short:

Pillow message: safe to ignore

Optimizer warning: safe to ignore for prediction; only matters if you resume training

1️⃣ Setup
import cv2
import numpy as np
from google.colab import files, output
from IPython.display import display, Javascript
from PIL import Image
import io
import base64

captured_image = None  # Will store the final processed image
2️⃣ Option A: Capture image from webcam
# Callback function to receive image from JS
def get_image(data):
    global captured_image
    image_bytes = base64.b64decode(data.split(',')[1])
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(image_bytes))
    img = np.array(img)
    img = cv2.resize(img, (224, 224))  # Resize like training
    img = img / 255.0                   # Normalize
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)   # Add batch dimension
    captured_image = img
    print("Webcam image captured and processed!")

output.register_callback('notebook.get_image', get_image)

def capture_from_webcam():
    display(Javascript('''
    async function capture(){
        const video = document.createElement('video');
        const stream = await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({video: true});
        video.srcObject = stream;
        await video.play();
        const canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
        canvas.width = video.videoWidth;
        canvas.height = video.videoHeight;
        canvas.getContext('2d').drawImage(video, 0, 0);
        const data = canvas.toDataURL('image/jpeg');
        google.colab.kernel.invokeFunction('notebook.get_image', [data], {});
        stream.getTracks().forEach(track => track.stop());
    }
    capture();
    '''))
Run:

capture_from_webcam()

3️⃣ Option B: Upload image manually
def upload_image():
    global captured_image
    uploaded = files.upload()
    for filename in uploaded.keys():
        img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(uploaded[filename]))
        img = np.array(img)
        img = cv2.resize(img, (224, 224))  # Resize like training
        img = img / 255.0                   # Normalize
        img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)   # Add batch dimension
        captured_image = img
        print(f"Image '{filename}' uploaded and processed!")

🔴 What the error means

You did not save the model, or

The model was saved in a different session, or

The file is on your local PC, not uploaded to Colab, or

The filename is different.

if the model is trained before weather can i train another time 
ChatGPT said:
Yes ✅ you can absolutely train the model again — and in your case, you SHOULD.

Let me explain clearly and confidently so you can also answer this in a viva.

✅ Short Answer
Yes.
Even if the model was trained before, you can:

Train it again

Train it multiple times

Improve accuracy by retraining

There is no problem at all.

🧠 Why retraining is OK (and normal)
1️⃣ Colab sessions reset
Old trained models are lost

Retraining is required

2️⃣ ML models improve with retraining
More epochs → better learning

Better preprocessing → better results

3️⃣ You may want to:
Change parameters

Add more data

Fix mistakes

🔁 Two retraining cases (important)
🟢 Case 1: You DON’T have a saved model
➡️ You MUST train again

model.fit(...)
🟡 Case 2: You DO have a saved model
You have two choices:

🔹 OPTION A: Train from scratch (recommended for students)
model = build_model()  # rebuild model
model.fit(...)
model.save("multimodal_model.keras")
✔ Clean learning
✔ Easy to explain
✔ Best for exams & projects

🔹 OPTION B: Continue training an old model (advanced)
model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")
model.fit(...)  # continues training
✔ Fine-tuning
❌ Harder to explain in viva

✅ What you MUST do before model.fit()

🟢 Correct order (VERY IMPORTANT)
1️⃣ Build model
2️⃣ Compile model
3️⃣ Train model
4️⃣ Save model
5️⃣ Predict

✅ STEP 1: Build the MULTIMODAL model (copy–paste fully)
from tensorflow.keras.applications import ResNet50
from tensorflow.keras.models import Model
from tensorflow.keras.layers import Input, Dense, Dropout, GlobalAveragePooling2D, Concatenate
from tensorflow.keras.optimizers import Adam

# -------- IMAGE BRANCH --------
image_input = Input(shape=(224, 224, 3), name="image_input")
base_model = ResNet50(weights="imagenet", include_top=False, input_tensor=image_input)
base_model.trainable = False

x = GlobalAveragePooling2D()(base_model.output)
x = Dense(128, activation="relu")(x)
x = Dropout(0.5)(x)

# -------- VOICE BRANCH --------
voice_input = Input(shape=(22,), name="voice_input")
v = Dense(64, activation="relu")(voice_input)
v = Dropout(0.5)(v)

# -------- MERGE --------
merged = Concatenate()([x, v])
merged = Dense(64, activation="relu")(merged)
output = Dense(1, activation="sigmoid")(merged)

model = Model(inputs=[image_input, voice_input], outputs=output)

# -------- COMPILE --------
model.compile(
    optimizer=Adam(learning_rate=0.0001),
    loss="binary_crossentropy",
    metrics=["accuracy"]
)

model.summary()
👉 If this runs without error → ✅ model is defined

✅ STEP 2: Train the model
history = model.fit(
    [X_img_train, Xv_train_aligned],
    y_img_train,
    validation_data=([X_img_test, Xv_test_aligned], y_img_test),
    epochs=20,
    batch_size=8
)
You MUST see:

Epoch 1/20
Epoch 2/20
...
🎉 Now the model is trained

🔹 STEP 1: Load image data
import tensorflow as tf

IMG_SIZE = (224, 224)
BATCH_SIZE = 8

train_ds = tf.keras.preprocessing.image_dataset_from_directory(
    "/content/data",
    validation_split=0.3,
    subset="training",
    seed=123,
    image_size=IMG_SIZE,
    batch_size=BATCH_SIZE
)

val_ds = tf.keras.preprocessing.image_dataset_from_directory(
    "/content/data",
    validation_split=0.3,
    subset="validation",
    seed=123,
    image_size=IMG_SIZE,
    batch_size=BATCH_SIZE
)
🔹 STEP 2: Convert datasets to NumPy arrays
import numpy as np

def dataset_to_numpy(dataset):
    images, labels = [], []
    for img, lbl in dataset:
        images.append(img.numpy())
        labels.append(lbl.numpy())
    return np.concatenate(images), np.concatenate(labels)

X_img_train, y_img_train = dataset_to_numpy(train_ds)
X_img_test, y_img_test = dataset_to_numpy(val_ds)

# Normalize
X_img_train = X_img_train / 255.0
X_img_test = X_img_test / 255.0
🔹 STEP 3: Verify shapes
print(X_img_train.shape)
print(y_img_train.shape)
print(X_img_test.shape)
print(y_img_test.shape)

(N, 224, 224, 3)
(N,)

(30, 22)

    epochs=20,

what dataset i need to upload image and voice as separate or the mulit-model
ChatGPT said:
This is an excellent and very important question 👍
I’ll explain it clearly in simple words, so you can also explain it in your project presentation / viva.

✅ Short Answer (very clear)
👉 You do NOT upload a “multimodal dataset” as one single file.
👉 You upload TWO SEPARATE datasets:

1️⃣ Image dataset
2️⃣ Voice (audio) dataset

Then YOU combine (merge) them during training using a multimodal model.

🧠 Why separate datasets?
Because:

Images and audio are different data types

They need different preprocessing

The model has two input branches

This is how real-world multimodal AI systems work.

📁 What EXACT datasets you need
🖼️ 1️⃣ IMAGE DATASET (REQUIRED)
Examples:
Spiral drawings

Handwriting samples

Facial images (optional)

Folder structure (VERY IMPORTANT):
/content/data_images/
├── healthy/
│   ├── img1.jpg
│   ├── img2.jpg
│   └── ...
└── parkinson/
    ├── img1.jpg
    ├── img2.jpg
    └── ...
✔ One image = one sample
✔ Folder name = class label

🎙️ 2️⃣ VOICE (AUDIO) DATASET (REQUIRED)
Examples:
Sustained vowel sounds

Speech recordings

Structure:
/content/data_voice/
├── healthy/
│   ├── audio1.wav
│   ├── audio2.wav
│   └── ...
└── parkinson/
    ├── audio1.wav
    ├── audio2.wav
    └── ...
✔ One audio file = one sample
✔ Extract MFCC features (e.g., 22 features)

🔗 How are they MERGED then?
👉 They are NOT merged at file level
👉 They are merged inside the neural network

During training:
model.fit(
   [X_img_train, X_voice_train],
   y_train
)
Inside the model:
Image CNN features  ─┐
                     ├─ Concatenate → Dense → Output
Voice MFCC features ─┘
🎯 VERY IMPORTANT RULE (must remember)
⚠️ The labels MUST match

That means:

Image #1 → Voice #1 → Same person → Same label

Image #72 → Voice #72 → Same class

If datasets are separate but aligned properly, multimodal learning works.

📊 Minimum dataset size (student-friendly)
Dataset	Minimum
Images	100+
Audio	100+
Per class	~50
🧠 Simple Viva Explanation (memorize this)
“In our Parkinson’s disease project, we use a multimodal approach where image and voice data are collected separately. Each data type is preprocessed independently and then combined at the feature level inside the neural network to improve prediction accuracy.”

Option 1: Quick “near real-time” in Colab (record → predict)
# Step 1: Install necessary libraries
!pip install librosa soundfile

import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from google.colab import files

# Step 2: Upload audio file
uploaded = files.upload()  # choose your voice sample

audio_path = list(uploaded.keys())[0]  # get uploaded file name

# Step 3: Extract features (MFCCs)
y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)  # first 5 sec
mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)

# Step 4: Prepare input for your model

# Step 5: Load your trained multimodal model

# Step 6: Predict

    print("🧠 Parkinson’s Disease Detected")

✅ This works in near real-time by uploading a new short audio clip each time.

Option 2: Real-time microphone prediction (local Python only)
# Install packages
pip install sounddevice scipy librosa tensorflow

import sounddevice as sd
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model

# Load model
model = load_model('multimodal_model.keras')

# Function to record audio
def record_audio(duration=5, sr=22050):
    print("Recording...")
    audio = sd.rec(int(duration*sr), samplerate=sr, channels=1)
    sd.wait()
    audio = audio.flatten()
    return audio, sr

# Function to predict
def predict_audio(audio, sr):
    mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=audio, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfccs = np.mean(mfccs.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)
    prediction = model.predict([np.zeros((1, 2048)), mfccs])
    prob = float(prediction[0][0])
    if prob >= 0.5:
        print("🧠 Parkinson’s Disease Detected")
    else:
        print("🧠 No Parkinson’s Disease Detected")
    print(f"Confidence: {prob*100:.2f}%")

# Record and predict
audio, sr = record_audio(duration=5)
predict_audio(audio, sr)
✅ This will record from your microphone and predict instantly.

Perfect! Once you have installed PortAudio and the Python packages (sounddevice, librosa, tensorflow, scipy), you can proceed to implement real-time voice prediction. Here’s the step-by-step workflow:

Step 1: Import libraries
import sounddevice as sd
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
Step 2: Load your trained model
model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")  # or your actual model path
Step 3: Record audio in real time
def record_audio(duration=5, sr=22050):
    print("Recording...")
    audio = sd.rec(int(duration * sr), samplerate=sr, channels=1)
    sd.wait()  # Wait until recording is finished
    print("Recording finished")
    audio = audio.flatten()
    return audio, sr
Step 4: Extract MFCC features
def extract_mfcc(audio, sr, n_mfcc=22):
    mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=audio, sr=sr, n_mfcc=n_mfcc)
    mfccs = np.mean(mfccs.T, axis=0)  # shape (22,)
    return mfccs.reshape(1, -1)  # shape (1, 22)
Step 5: Make prediction
audio, sr = record_audio(duration=5)
mfcc_features = extract_mfcc(audio, sr)

prediction = model.predict([mfcc_features])  # or your multimodal input format
prob = float(prediction[0][0])

if prob >= 0.5:
    print("🧠 Parkinson’s Disease Detected")
else:
    print("🧠 No Parkinson’s Disease Detected")

print(f"Confidence: {prob * 100:.2f}%")

/usr/local/lib/python3.12/dist-packages/keras/src/saving/saving_lib.py:802: UserWarning: Skipping variable loading for optimizer 'adam', because it has 18 variables whereas the saved optimizer has 2 variables. 
  saveable.load_own_variables(weights_store.get(inner_path))
ChatGPT said:
Ah! That warning is normal and not critical.

Here’s what it means:

When you load a Keras model using load_model(), it tries to also restore the optimizer state (like Adam’s internal momentum variables).

If your saved model’s optimizer has a different number of variables than the current Keras version expects, Keras will skip loading the optimizer variables.

Your model weights (the actual neural network parameters) are still loaded correctly, so predictions will work perfectly.

In short: You can safely ignore this warning if you only want to do inference (prediction) and not continue training.

If you want, I can give you a clean way to load the model for inference so this warning doesn’t even appear. Do you want me to show that?

PortAudioError: Error querying device -1
ChatGPT said:
Ah! That error is coming from sounddevice, not your model.

What it means:
PortAudioError: Error querying device -1 occurs when Python cannot access a microphone.

In Colab, Kaggle, or other cloud notebooks, you cannot record audio directly, because there’s no physical mic available.

Solutions:
For local machine (Windows/Mac/Linux):

Make sure you have a working microphone.

Test with:

import sounddevice as sd
print(sd.query_devices())  # List all audio devices
Then use the correct device number in sd.rec():

audio = sd.rec(int(duration*sr), samplerate=sr, channels=1, device=1)
For Colab / cloud notebooks:

You cannot use sounddevice.

Alternative: let the user upload an audio file instead:

from google.colab import files
uploaded = files.upload()  # User uploads voice_sample.wav
audio_path = list(uploaded.keys())[0]
Then process it with librosa:

import librosa
y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)

 ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
NameError                                 Traceback (most recent call last)

NameError: name 'duration' is not defined
ChatGPT said:
Ah! That’s because duration and sr haven’t been defined before calling sd.rec(). In Python, you must define variables first. For example:

import sounddevice as sd

duration = 5  # seconds
sr = 22050    # sampling rate
device = 1    # your microphone device number (check with sd.query_devices())

print("Recording...")
audio = sd.rec(int(duration * sr), samplerate=sr, channels=1, device=device)
sd.wait()  # Wait until recording is finished
print("Recording finished!")
💡 Key points:

ChatGPT said:
Ah! This error happens because the device index you’re using is not valid. Some key points:

device=1 may not exist on your system. The number depends on your microphones/devices.

PortAudio can’t query the device, so recording fails.

This always needs a local machine—it won’t work on Google Colab or cloud notebooks because they don’t have access to your microphone.

Here’s how to fix it:

import sounddevice as sd

# List all available audio devices

sr = 22050    # sampling rate

sd.wait()

PortAudioError: Error querying device -1
ChatGPT said:
Ah! This error clearly shows that the environment you are using doesn’t have access to a microphone.

Some key points:

device=-1 means "default device," but in Google Colab or cloud notebooks, there is no microphone available, so PortAudio cannot open any input device.

sounddevice and real-time audio recording only work on a local machine (Windows, macOS, Linux) where your microphone is connected.

✅ What you can do:

Option 1 – Local Python script:
Run the real-time recording code on your laptop/desktop. For example:

import sounddevice as sd
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model

# Load your trained model
model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")

# Recording function
def record_audio(duration=5, sr=22050):
    print("Recording...")
    audio = sd.rec(int(duration*sr), samplerate=sr, channels=1)
    sd.wait()
    print("Recording finished!")
    return audio.flatten(), sr

# MFCC extraction
def extract_mfcc(audio, sr):
    mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=audio, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    return np.mean(mfccs.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

# Record and predict
audio, sr = record_audio(duration=5)
mfcc_features = extract_mfcc(audio, sr)
prediction = model.predict([mfcc_features])
prob = float(prediction[0][0])

if prob >= 0.5:
    print("🧠 Parkinson’s Disease Detected")
else:
    print("🧠 No Parkinson’s Disease Detected")
print(f"Confidence: {prob*100:.2f}%")
Option 2 – Colab / Cloud Notebook:
You cannot do real-time recording. You must upload a .wav file instead:

from google.colab import files
uploaded = files.upload()
audio_path = list(uploaded.keys())[0]
y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
# Then extract MFCC and predict
💡 In short:
For real-time voice prediction, you must run the code locally, not on Colab or other cloud notebooks.

ChatGPT said:
Ah — now I see exactly what happened.

The error occurs because you are trying to load a ZIP file with librosa, which only supports audio files (.wav, .mp3, .flac, etc.). In your code:

audio_path = "23849127.zip"
y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
librosa cannot read .zip files, so it fails with LibsndfileError → NoBackendError.

✅ How to fix it
Unzip your file first to get the actual audio files:

import zipfile
import os

zip_path = "23849127.zip"
extract_dir = "audio_data"

with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, 'r') as zip_ref:
    zip_ref.extractall(extract_dir)

# List extracted files
os.listdir(extract_dir)
Load the actual .wav or .mp3 file:

import librosa
audio_file = "audio_data/voice_sample.wav"  # update with the extracted file name

y, sr = librosa.load(audio_file, duration=5)
Then extract MFCCs and predict as before:

import numpy as np

prediction = model.predict([mfcc_features])

if prob >= 0.5:
    print("🧠 Parkinson’s Disease Detected")
else:
    print("🧠 No Parkinson’s Disease Detected")

print(f"Confidence: {prob*100:.2f}%")

/**
 * @fileoverview Helpers for google.colab Python module.
 */
(function(scope) {
function span(text, styleAttributes = {}) {
  const element = document.createElement('span');
  element.textContent = text;
  for (const key of Object.keys(styleAttributes)) {
    element.style[key] = styleAttributes[key];
  }
  return element;
}

// Max number of bytes which will be uploaded at a time.
const MAX_PAYLOAD_SIZE = 100 * 1024;

function _uploadFiles(inputId, outputId) {
  const steps = uploadFilesStep(inputId, outputId);
  const outputElement = document.getElementById(outputId);
  // Cache steps on the outputElement to make it available for the next call
  // to uploadFilesContinue from Python.
  outputElement.steps = steps;

  return _uploadFilesContinue(outputId);
}

// This is roughly an async generator (not supported in the browser yet),
// where there are multiple asynchronous steps and the Python side is going
// to poll for completion of each step.
// This uses a Promise to block the python side on completion of each step,
// then passes the result of the previous step as the input to the next step.
function _uploadFilesContinue(outputId) {
  const outputElement = document.getElementById(outputId);
  const steps = outputElement.steps;

  const next = steps.next(outputElement.lastPromiseValue);
  return Promise.resolve(next.value.promise).then((value) => {
    // Cache the last promise value to make it available to the next
    // step of the generator.
    outputElement.lastPromiseValue = value;
    return next.value.response;
  });
}

/**
 * Generator function which is called between each async step of the upload
 * process.
 * @param {string} inputId Element ID of the input file picker element.
 * @param {string} outputId Element ID of the output display.
 * @return {!Iterable<!Object>} Iterable of next steps.
 */
function* uploadFilesStep(inputId, outputId) {
  const inputElement = document.getElementById(inputId);
  inputElement.disabled = false;

  const outputElement = document.getElementById(outputId);
  outputElement.innerHTML = '';

  const pickedPromise = new Promise((resolve) => {
    inputElement.addEventListener('change', (e) => {
      resolve(e.target.files);
    });
  });

  const cancel = document.createElement('button');
  inputElement.parentElement.appendChild(cancel);
  cancel.textContent = 'Cancel upload';
  const cancelPromise = new Promise((resolve) => {
    cancel.onclick = () => {
      resolve(null);
    };
  });

  // Wait for the user to pick the files.
  const files = yield {
    promise: Promise.race([pickedPromise, cancelPromise]),
    response: {
      action: 'starting',
    }
  };

  cancel.remove();

  // Disable the input element since further picks are not allowed.
  inputElement.disabled = true;

  if (!files) {
    return {
      response: {
        action: 'complete',
      }
    };
  }

  for (const file of files) {
    const li = document.createElement('li');
    li.append(span(file.name, {fontWeight: 'bold'}));
    li.append(span(
        (${file.type || 'n/a'}) - ${file.size} bytes,  +
        last modified: ${
            file.lastModifiedDate ? file.lastModifiedDate.toLocaleDateString() :
                                    'n/a'} - ));
    const percent = span('0% done');
    li.appendChild(percent);

    outputElement.appendChild(li);

    const fileDataPromise = new Promise((resolve) => {
      const reader = new FileReader();
      reader.onload = (e) => {
        resolve(e.target.result);
      };
      reader.readAsArrayBuffer(file);
    });
    // Wait for the data to be ready.
    let fileData = yield {
      promise: fileDataPromise,
      response: {
        action: 'continue',
      }
    };

    // Use a chunked sending to avoid message size limits. See b/62115660.
    let position = 0;
    do {
      const length = Math.min(fileData.byteLength - position, MAX_PAYLOAD_SIZE);
      const chunk = new Uint8Array(fileData, position, length);
      position += length;

      const base64 = btoa(String.fromCharCode.apply(null, chunk));
      yield {
        response: {
          action: 'append',
          file: file.name,
          data: base64,
        },
      };

      let percentDone = fileData.byteLength === 0 ?
          100 :
          Math.round((position / fileData.byteLength) * 100);
      percent.textContent = ${percentDone}% done;

    } while (position < fileData.byteLength);
  }

  // All done.
  yield {
    response: {
      action: 'complete',
    }
  };
}

scope.google = scope.google || {};
scope.google.colab = scope.google.colab || {};
scope.google.colab._files = {
  _uploadFiles,
  _uploadFilesContinue,
};
})(self);

Since you want to test a single audio file on Google Colab, here’s a simple example using librosa to load one .wav file and extract features (like MFCC) for your model:

import librosa
import numpy as np
import os

# Path to the audio folder
audio_folder = "/content/PD_AH/PD_AH"

# Pick one audio file to test
test_audio = "AH_545834603-857E007F-1CCF-4249-8160-3A0F3F5AB58D.wav"
audio_path = os.path.join(audio_folder, test_audio)

# Load the audio
y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, sr=22050)  # sr=22050 is default

# Extract MFCC features (example)
mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
mfcc_features = np.mean(mfccs.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

print("MFCC feature shape:", mfcc_features.shape)

# Now you can pass mfcc_features to your trained model
# prediction = model.predict(mfcc_features)
# print("Prediction:", prediction)

ChatGPT said:
Ah! Now the error makes sense. 🧐

Your model expects 2 inputs, but you are only providing the MFCC features (1 input). This is common in multimodal models, where one input might be MFCC/audio features and the other could be something like voice embeddings, spectrogram features, or metadata.

Here’s what you need to do:

Check your model summary to see the expected inputs:

model.summary()
You’ll see something like:

Input 1: shape=(None, 22)   # MFCC
Input 2: shape=(None, 2048) # e.g., image embeddings or other features
Prepare both inputs before prediction. For testing a single audio file, you might need to:

Extract MFCC features → shape (1, 22) ✅

Prepare the second input (e.g., zeros or a placeholder if you just want to test the audio path) → shape (1, 2048) or whatever your model expects.

Example for a placeholder:

import numpy as np

# MFCC features
mfcc_features = mfcc_features  # shape (1, 22)

# Second input placeholder (change shape according to your model)
second_input = np.zeros((1, 2048))  

# Predict
prediction = model.predict([mfcc_features, second_input])
print("Prediction:", prediction)

1️⃣ Prepare your inputs
Voice (MFCC features): shape (1, 22)

Image: preprocessed to shape (1, 224, 224, 3)

Example:

import numpy as np
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image

# Example: Load and preprocess your image
img_path = "path_to_image.jpg"
img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224, 224))
img_array = image.img_to_array(img)
img_array = np.expand_dims(img_array, axis=0)  # shape: (1, 224, 224, 3)
img_array = img_array / 255.0  # normalize

# Example: Voice features (MFCC)
# mfcc_features should already be shape (1, 22)
2️⃣ Predict using the multi-input model
# Make prediction
prediction = model.predict([img_array, mfcc_features])
prediction will be a probability between 0 and 1.

For example, 0.999999 → very high confidence the person has the disease (if 1 = disease).

3️⃣ Convert prediction to text with confidence
threshold = 0.5  # adjust according to your model

if prediction[0][0] >= threshold:
    result_text = "Person likely has the disease"
else:
    result_text = "Person likely does NOT have the disease"

confidence = prediction[0][0]  # value between 0 and 1
confidence_percent = confidence * 100

print(f"Prediction: {result_text}")
print(f"Confidence: {confidence_percent:.2f}%")
✅ Output example:

ChatGPT said:
Ah! I understand clearly. You want a step-by-step workflow where both image and voice are processed together, and the final output shows one combined prediction like:

Prediction: Person likely has the disease
Confidence: 99.99%
Here’s a clean way to do it in Python using Keras/TensorFlow (assuming you already have image_model and voice_model trained):

Step 1: Load and preprocess image
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import numpy as np
import os

# Image path
img_path = "path_to_image.jpg"

if not os.path.exists(img_path):
    raise FileNotFoundError(f"Image file not found: {img_path}")

# Load and preprocess image
img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224, 224))
img_array = image.img_to_array(img)
img_array = np.expand_dims(img_array, axis=0)  # shape: (1, 224, 224, 3)
img_array = img_array / 255.0  # normalize if model expects
Step 2: Load and preprocess voice
import librosa

# Voice path
voice_path = "path_to_voice.wav"

if not os.path.exists(voice_path):
    raise FileNotFoundError(f"Voice file not found: {voice_path}")

# Load audio and extract features (e.g., MFCC)
y, sr = librosa.load(voice_path, sr=22050)
mfccs = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=40)
mfccs_scaled = np.mean(mfccs.T, axis=0)
voice_array = np.expand_dims(mfccs_scaled, axis=0)  # shape: (1, 40)
Step 3: Make predictions
# Predict separately
image_pred = image_model.predict(img_array)  # returns probability
voice_pred = voice_model.predict(voice_array)  # returns probability

# Combine predictions (simple average)
combined_pred = (image_pred + voice_pred) / 2.0
Step 4: Display final output
threshold = 0.5  # adjust based on your model

if combined_pred >= threshold:
    prediction_text = "Person likely has the disease"
else:
    prediction_text = "Person likely does not have the disease"

confidence = combined_pred[0][0] * 100

print(f"Prediction: {prediction_text}")
print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}%")
✅ This way:

You input image + voice together

Model predictions are combined into one final probability

Output is clear text + confidence %

🟢 OPTIONAL: Put Everything into ONE FUNCTION
def predict_parkinsons(img_path, audio_path):
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224, 224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    pred = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(pred[0][0]) * 100

    if confidence >= 50:
        result = "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease"
    else:
        result = "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"

    print("Prediction:", result)
    print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}%")

✅ FINAL GOAL (WHAT THIS CODE DOES)
✔ Takes ONE image + ONE voice file

Prediction: Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease

✅ FINAL WORKING CODE (COPY–PASTE FULLY)
🔹 STEP 1: Imports
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
🔹 STEP 2: Prediction Function (IMAGE + VOICE TOGETHER)
def predict_parkinsons(img_path, audio_path, model, threshold=0.5):
    
    # -------- IMAGE PREPROCESSING --------
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224, 224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)   # (1, 224, 224, 3)
    
    # -------- AUDIO PREPROCESSING --------
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0)
    mfcc = mfcc.reshape(1, -1)          # (1, 22)
    
    # -------- MODEL PREDICTION --------
    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0])
    confidence_percent = confidence * 100
    
    # -------- TEXT OUTPUT --------
    if confidence >= threshold:
        print("Prediction: Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease")
    else:
        print("Prediction: Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease")
    
    print(f"Confidence: {confidence_percent:.2f}%")
🔹 STEP 3: CALL THE FUNCTION (ONE COMMAND)
img_path = "/content/sample_image.jpg"  # <-- put your image here
audio_path = "/content/PD_AH/PD_AH/AH_545834603-857E007F-1CCF-4249-8160-3A0F3F5AB58D.wav"

predict_parkinsons(img_path, audio_path, model)

✅ STEP 3: FINAL IMAGE + VOICE PREDICTION FUNCTION (WORKING)
🔹 This function:
• Takes image + voice
• Uses 2-input trained model
• Gives human-readable output
• Shows confidence %

import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image

def predict_parkinsons(img_path, audio_path, model, threshold=0.5):

    # -------- IMAGE PREPROCESSING --------
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224, 224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)   # (1, 224, 224, 3)

    # -------- AUDIO PREPROCESSING --------
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0)
    mfcc = mfcc.reshape(1, -1)          # (1, 22)

    # -------- PREDICTION --------
    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])

    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    # -------- OUTPUT --------
    if confidence >= threshold * 100:
        print("Prediction: Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease")
    else:
        print("Prediction: Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease")

    print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}%")
✅ STEP 4: CALL THE FUNCTION (ONE COMMAND)
img_path = "/content/spiral_test.jpg"
audio_path = "/content/PD_AH/PD_AH/AH_545834603-857E007F-1CCF-4249-8160-3A0F3F5AB58D.wav"

predict_parkinsons(img_path, audio_path, model)

🔷 app.py (BACKEND CODE)
👉 This replaces Google Colab

from flask import Flask, request, jsonify
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import os

app = Flask(__name__)
UPLOAD_FOLDER = "uploads"
os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")

@app.route("/predict", methods=["POST"])
def predict():
    img_file = request.files["image"]
    audio_file = request.files["audio"]

    img_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, img_file.filename)
    audio_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, audio_file.filename)

    img_file.save(img_path)
    audio_file.save(audio_path)

    # IMAGE
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224,224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    # AUDIO
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    if confidence >= 50:
        result = "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease"
    else:
        result = "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"

    return jsonify({
        "prediction": result,
        "confidence": f"{confidence:.2f}%"
    })

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app.run(debug=True)
🔷 STEP 3: RUN BACKEND SERVER
python app.py
Server will run at:

http://127.0.0.1:5000/predict
🔷 STEP 4: FRONTEND (WEBSITE)

<!DOCTYPE html>

    <title>Parkinson’s Detection</title>
    <link rel="stylesheet" href="style.css">
</head>
<body>

<h1>Parkinson’s Disease Detection</h1>

<input type="file" id="image">
<input type="file" id="audio">

<button onclick="predict()">Predict</button>

<h2 id="output"></h2>

<script src="script.js"></script>
</body>
</html>
🔹 script.js (THIS CONNECTS FRONTEND → BACKEND)
function predict() {
    let image = document.getElementById("image").files[0];
    let audio = document.getElementById("audio").files[0];

    let formData = new FormData();
    formData.append("image", image);
    formData.append("audio", audio);

    fetch("http://127.0.0.1:5000/predict", {
        method: "POST",
        body: formData
    })
    .then(response => response.json())
    .then(data => {
        document.getElementById("output").innerHTML =
            `${data.prediction}<br>Confidence: ${data.confidence}`;
    })
    .catch(err => {
        alert("Error connecting to backend");
    });
}
🔹 style.css (OPTIONAL)
body {
    text-align: center;
    font-family: Arial;
    background: #f2f2f2;
}

button {
    padding: 10px 20px;
    font-size: 16px;
}

from flask import Flask, request, jsonify
from flask_ngrok import run_with_ngrok
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import os

app = Flask(__name__)
run_with_ngrok(app)  # <-- VERY IMPORTANT

UPLOAD_FOLDER = "/content/uploads"
os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

model = load_model("/content/multimodal_model.keras")

@app.route("/predict", methods=["POST"])
def predict():

    img_file = request.files["image"]
    audio_file = request.files["audio"]

    img_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, img_file.filename)
    audio_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, audio_file.filename)

    img_file.save(img_path)
    audio_file.save(audio_path)

    # -------- IMAGE --------
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224,224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    # -------- AUDIO --------
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    if confidence >= 50:
        result = "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease"
    else:
        result = "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"

    return jsonify({
        "prediction": result,
        "confidence": f"{confidence:.2f}%"
    })

app.run()

🔹 script.js (IMPORTANT PART)
📌 THIS IS WHERE BACKEND DATA IS FETCHED
function predict() {

  let image = document.getElementById("image").files[0];
  let audio = document.getElementById("audio").files[0];

  let formData = new FormData();
  formData.append("image", image);
  formData.append("audio", audio);

  fetch("https://abcd1234.ngrok.io/predict", {   // <-- COLAB URL
    method: "POST",
    body: formData
  })
  .then(response => response.json())
  .then(data => {
    document.getElementById("result").innerHTML =
      data.prediction + "<br>Confidence: " + data.confidence;
  })
  .catch(error => {
    alert("Backend connection failed");
  });
}
⚠️ Replace abcd1234.ngrok.io with your Colab URL

from flask import Flask, request, jsonify
from flask_ngrok import run_with_ngrok
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import os

app = Flask(__name__)
run_with_ngrok(app)  # <-- VERY IMPORTANT

UPLOAD_FOLDER = "/content/uploads"
os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

model = load_model("/content/multimodal_model.keras")

@app.route("/predict", methods=["POST"])
def predict():

    img_file = request.files["image"]
    audio_file = request.files["audio"]

    img_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, img_file.filename)
    audio_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, audio_file.filename)

    img_file.save(img_path)
    audio_file.save(audio_path)

    # -------- IMAGE --------
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224,224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    # -------- AUDIO --------
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    if confidence >= 50:
        result = "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease"
    else:
        result = "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"

    return jsonify({
        "prediction": result,
        "confidence": f"{confidence:.2f}%"
    })

from flask import Flask, request, jsonify
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import os
from pyngrok import ngrok

app = Flask(__name__)

UPLOAD_FOLDER = "/content/uploads"
os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

model = load_model("/content/multimodal_model.keras")

@app.route("/predict", methods=["POST"])
def predict():
    img_file = request.files["image"]
    audio_file = request.files["audio"]

    img_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, img_file.filename)
    audio_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, audio_file.filename)

    img_file.save(img_path)
    audio_file.save(audio_path)

    # -------- IMAGE --------
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224,224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    # -------- AUDIO --------
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    if confidence >= 50:
        result = "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease"
    else:
        result = "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"

    return jsonify({
        "prediction": result,
        "confidence": f"{confidence:.2f}%"
    })

# 🔹 Start ngrok tunnel
public_url = ngrok.connect(5000)
print("PUBLIC URL:", public_url)

app.run(port=5000)

from flask import Flask, request, jsonify
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import os
from pyngrok import ngrok

ngrok.set_auth_token("YOUR_NGROK_AUTH_TOKEN")

app = Flask(__name__)

UPLOAD_FOLDER = "/content/uploads"
os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

model = load_model("/content/multimodal_model.keras")

@app.route("/predict", methods=["POST"])
def predict():
    img_file = request.files["image"]
    audio_file = request.files["audio"]

    img_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, img_file.filename)
    audio_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, audio_file.filename)

    img_file.save(img_path)
    audio_file.save(audio_path)

    # IMAGE
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224,224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    # AUDIO
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    result = (
        "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease"
        if confidence >= 50
        else "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"
    )

    return jsonify({
        "prediction": result,
        "confidence": f"{confidence:.2f}%"
    })

public_url = ngrok.connect(5000)
print("PUBLIC URL:", public_url)

app.run(port=5000)

<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
  <meta charset="UTF-8">
  <title>Parkinson Disease Detection</title>
  <style>
    body {
      font-family: Arial;
      background: #0f2027;
      background: linear-gradient(to right, #2c5364, #203a43, #0f2027);
      color: white;
      text-align: center;
      padding: 50px;
    }
    input, button {
      padding: 10px;
      margin: 10px;
    }
    button {
      background: #00c6ff;
      border: none;
      cursor: pointer;
    }
    #result {
      margin-top: 20px;
      font-size: 20px;
    }
  </style>
</head>
<body>

  <h1>🧠 Parkinson Disease Detection</h1>

  <form id="uploadForm">
    <label>Upload Spiral Image</label><br>
    <input type="file" id="image" accept="image/*" required><br>

    <label>Upload Voice File</label><br>
    <input type="file" id="audio" accept="audio/*" required><br>

    <button type="submit">Predict</button>
  </form>

  <div id="result"></div>

  <script>
    const form = document.getElementById("uploadForm");

    form.addEventListener("submit", async (e) => {
      e.preventDefault();

      const imageFile = document.getElementById("image").files[0];
      const audioFile = document.getElementById("audio").files[0];

      const formData = new FormData();
      formData.append("image", imageFile);
      formData.append("audio", audioFile);

      document.getElementById("result").innerHTML = "⏳ Predicting...";

      try {
        const response = await fetch(
          "https://harsh-omer-undemolished.ngrok-free.dev/predict",
          {
            method: "POST",
            body: formData
          }
        );

        const data = await response.json();

        document.getElementById("result").innerHTML = `
          <strong>Prediction:</strong> ${data.prediction}<br>
          <strong>Confidence:</strong> ${data.confidence}
        `;
      } catch (error) {
        document.getElementById("result").innerHTML =
          "❌ Error connecting to server";
      }
    });
  </script>

</body>
</html>

Ah! this part is important. Let me explain clearly.

The ngrok public URL is what your frontend uses to talk to your backend.

1️⃣ Where to use it
In your index.html JavaScript, you have this line:

const response = await fetch(
  "https://harsh-omer-undemolished.ngrok-free.dev/predict",
  {
    method: "POST",
    body: formData
  }
);
"https://harsh-omer-undemolished.ngrok-free.dev/predict" → THIS IS THE PLACE WHERE YOU PUT YOUR NGROK URL

Make sure to include /predict at the end because that is your Flask API endpoint.

2️⃣ How it works
User uploads image + audio in the website.

JS sends a POST request to your ngrok URL (fetch()).

Flask backend receives the files at /predict, runs your ML model.

Flask sends JSON response back (prediction + confidence).

JS displays the results in the frontend.

3️⃣ What happens if you change the ngrok URL
Every time you restart Colab, ngrok URL changes (unless you have paid ngrok account).

You must update this URL in your frontend code (fetch() call) every time.

✅ Summary

Use ngrok URL in your frontend’s fetch POST request.

Always include the endpoint /predict after the ngrok domain.

Perfect! Let’s create a ready-to-use Replit setup for your Parkinson’s project. I’ll outline all the code files you’ll need and how they connect:

1️⃣ Folder Structure

from flask import Flask, request, jsonify, render_template
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import os
from pyngrok import ngrok

app = Flask(__name__)
UPLOAD_FOLDER = "uploads"
os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

# Load your pretrained model
model = load_model("multimodal_model.keras")

@app.route("/")
def home():
    return render_template("index.html")

@app.route("/predict", methods=["POST"])
def predict():
    img_file = request.files["image"]
    audio_file = request.files["audio"]

    img_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, img_file.filename)
    audio_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, audio_file.filename)

    img_file.save(img_path)
    audio_file.save(audio_path)

    # Image preprocessing
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224,224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    # Audio preprocessing
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    # Prediction
    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100
    result = "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease" if confidence >= 50 else "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"

    return jsonify({"prediction": result, "confidence": f"{confidence:.2f}%"})

# Start ngrok tunnel
public_url = ngrok.connect(5000)
print("PUBLIC URL:", public_url)

app.run(port=5000)

        <label>Upload Image:</label>
        <input type="file" name="image" required><br><br>
        <label>Upload Audio:</label>
        <input type="file" name="audio" required><br><br>
        <button type="submit">Predict</button>
    </form>

    <h2 id="result"></h2>
    <script>
        const form = document.getElementById("predict-form");
        form.addEventListener("submit", async (e) => {
            e.preventDefault();
            const formData = new FormData(form);
            const response = await fetch("/predict", {
                method: "POST",
                body: formData
            });
            const data = await response.json();
            document.getElementById("result").innerText = `${data.prediction} (Confidence: ${data.confidence})`;
        });
    </script>
</body>
</html>

from flask import Flask, request, jsonify, send_file
import numpy as np
import librosa
from tensorflow.keras.models import load_model
from tensorflow.keras.preprocessing import image
import os
from pyngrok import ngrok
from reportlab.lib.pagesizes import A4
from reportlab.pdfgen import canvas
from datetime import datetime

app = Flask(__name__)

UPLOAD_FOLDER = "/content/uploads"
REPORT_FOLDER = "/content/reports"

os.makedirs(UPLOAD_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)
os.makedirs(REPORT_FOLDER, exist_ok=True)

# 🔹 Load Model
model = load_model("/content/multimodal_model.keras")

# 🔹 Prediction API
@app.route("/predict", methods=["POST"])
def predict():
    img_file = request.files["image"]
    audio_file = request.files["audio"]

    img_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, img_file.filename)
    audio_path = os.path.join(UPLOAD_FOLDER, audio_file.filename)

    img_file.save(img_path)
    audio_file.save(audio_path)

    # -------- IMAGE --------
    img = image.load_img(img_path, target_size=(224,224))
    img = image.img_to_array(img) / 255.0
    img = np.expand_dims(img, axis=0)

    # -------- AUDIO --------
    y, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, duration=5)
    mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=sr, n_mfcc=22)
    mfcc = np.mean(mfcc.T, axis=0).reshape(1, -1)

    prediction = model.predict([img, mfcc])
    confidence = float(prediction[0][0]) * 100

    if confidence >= 50:
        result = "Person likely HAS Parkinson’s Disease"
    else:
        result = "Person likely does NOT have Parkinson’s Disease"

    # 🔹 Stage logic
    if confidence < 65:
        stage = "Early Stage"
    elif confidence < 80:
        stage = "Mid Stage"
    else:
        stage = "Advanced Stage"

    return jsonify({
        "prediction": result,
        "confidence": round(confidence, 2),
        "stage": stage
    })

# 🔹 PDF REPORT API
@app.route("/download-report", methods=["POST"])
def download_report():
    data = request.json

    prediction = data["prediction"]
    confidence = data["confidence"]
    stage = data["stage"]

    filename = f"Parkinson_Report_{datetime.now().strftime('%Y%m%d_%H%M%S')}.pdf"
    file_path = os.path.join(REPORT_FOLDER, filename)

    c = canvas.Canvas(file_path, pagesize=A4)
    width, height = A4

    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 18)
    c.drawString(50, height - 50, "Parkinson’s Disease Detection Report")

    c.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    c.drawString(50, height - 100, f"Prediction Result: {prediction}")
    c.drawString(50, height - 130, f"Confidence: {confidence}%")
    c.drawString(50, height - 160, f"Disease Stage: {stage}")
    c.drawString(50, height - 190, f"Generated On: {datetime.now().strftime('%d-%m-%Y %H:%M:%S')}")

    c.setFont("Helvetica-Oblique", 10)
    c.drawString(50, height - 240, "Disclaimer:")
    c.drawString(50, height - 260, 
        "This report is generated using an AI system and is not a medical diagnosis.")
    c.drawString(50, height - 280, 
        "Please consult a certified neurologist for professional advice.")

    c.showPage()
    c.save()

    return send_file(file_path, as_attachment=True)

# 🔹 Start ngrok
public_url = ngrok.connect(5000)
print("PUBLIC URL:", public_url)

app.run(port=5000)
🌐 STEP 3: HOW FRONTEND WILL DOWNLOAD PDF
After getting prediction response, send data like this 👇

fetch("https://YOUR_NGROK_URL/download-report", {
  method: "POST",
  headers: {
    "Content-Type": "application/json"
  },
  body: JSON.stringify({
    prediction: result,
    confidence: confidence,
    stage: stage
  })
})
.then(res => res.blob())
.then(blob => {
  const url = window.URL.createObjectURL(blob);
  const a = document.createElement("a");
  a.href = url;
  a.download = "Parkinson_Report.pdf";
  a.click();
});

2️⃣ Explanation of Important Voice Features (Columns)
🔹 Frequency Features (Voice Pitch)
MDVP:Fo(Hz) → Average vocal pitch

MDVP:Fhi(Hz) → Highest pitch

🔹 Jitter Features (Voice Trembling / Instability)

🔹 Noise-related Features
NHR (Noise-to-Harmonics Ratio)

HNR (Harmonics-to-Noise Ratio)

✔ Parkinson’s voice contains more noise
✔ NHR increases, HNR decreases

🔹 Nonlinear / Advanced Voice Features
RPDE → Measures randomness in vocal fold vibrations

DFA → Measures voice signal stability

✔ Parkinson’s disease → less stable and more random voice patterns

🔹 Target Column (Label)
status

👉 This is the output label your ML model learns to predict.
